# Higham Chapter 13 Formalization Report

## Source and Scope

- Edition: 2nd ed., SIAM, 2002, verified from repository metadata and PDF chapter numbering.
- Chapter: 13, "Block LU Factorization"
- Printed pages: 245--258
- Source file: `References/1.9780898718027.ch13.pdf`
- Mode: core
- Parallel split: 3
- Planning documents consulted: blueprint, split-3 contract, chapter index
- Inventory path: `docs/CHAPTER13_SOURCE_INVENTORY.md`
- Proof-source ledger: `docs/CHAPTER13_PROOF_SOURCE_LEDGER.md`
- Bottleneck ledger: `docs/CHAPTER13_BOTTLENECK_LEDGER.md`
- Selected-scope gate: FAIL, because the current Lean module contains useful Chapter 13 scaffolding but not complete source-faithful proofs for all selected targets.

## Current Lean State Before New Implementation

The existing module `LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LU/BlockLU.lean` is the right home for Chapter 13 block-LU work. It already contains:

| Source target | Current declaration | Current assessment |
|---|---|---|
| Block LU factorization definition | `BlockLUFactSpec` | Useful dependency; source labels corrected to Chapter 13. |
| Chapter 13 norm convention | `higham13_norm_convention_blockMaxNorm_eq_entrywise_sup`, `block_entry_abs_le_blockMaxNorm`, `blockMaxNorm_le_of_entry_abs_le`, `higham13_block_norm_eq_maxEntryNorm` | Exact entrywise block-index form of the chapter's max norm and utility bounds; `higham13_block_norm_eq_maxEntryNorm` proves that the ambient Pi norm on `Fin r -> Fin r -> R` blocks is the same max-entry norm used by the Algorithm 13.3 stage tables. No separate quotient-based flat `Fin (m*r)` API is introduced. |
| Block LU to standard LU prose bridge | `higham13_standardUpperFromBlockUpper`, `higham13_block_upper_refinement_eq`, `higham13_block_lu_to_standard_lu_product` | Exact flat product identity using diagonal-block LU refinements; it does not by itself prove the lower/upper triangular shape of the refined factors. |

| Eq.13.20/Eq.13.26 partition displays | `higham13_eq13_20_partition`, `higham13_eq13_26_partition` | Exact source-facing wrappers around Mathlib `Matrix.fromBlocks_toBlocks`; Eq.13.26 records the `A11` invertibility assumption for later Problem 13.4 work, but does not prove Problem 13.4's norm or condition-number inequalities. |
| SPD symmetric partition, Schur positive-definiteness, and block-LU existence route | `higham13_spd_symmetric_partition_isSymm`, `higham13_spd_leadingBlock_posDef`, `higham13_spd_schurComplement_posDef`, `higham13_spd_schurComplement_posDef_of_full`, `higham13_spd_schurComplement_source_posDef`, `blockMatrixFlat`, `blockMatrixNonsingular_of_flat_inverse`, `blockMatrixNonsingular_of_isUnit_det_flat`, `blockMatrixNonsingular_of_det_ne_zero_flat`, `blockMatrixNonsingular_of_posDef_flat`, `matrix_posDef_submatrix_of_injective`, `blockMatrixFlat_leadingBlockPrefix13_2`, `leadingBlockPrefix13_2_posDef_flat_of_posDef_flat`, `LeadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2.of_posDef_flat`, `BlockLUFactSpec.existsUnique_of_posDef_flat` | Exact `Matrix.fromBlocks` symmetry wrapper for the display `[[A11,A21ᵀ],[A21,A22]]`; `higham13_spd_leadingBlock_posDef` proves the leading block is positive definite, and `higham13_spd_schurComplement_source_posDef` proves the printed real Schur complement `A22 - A21 A11⁻¹ A21ᵀ` is positive definite from the full block SPD hypothesis. In addition, flat positive definiteness of the uniform block matrix now implies all leading block prefixes are flat-SPD, hence block-nonsingular, and Theorem 13.2 gives a unique block LU factorization. Lemma 13.9 is closed by the exact source-facing theorem, and Lemma 13.10 is closed by `higham13_lemma13_10_schur_kappa_bound_of_spd`; downstream scalar stability packaging remains conditional on the displayed product/backward-error premises. |
| Algorithm 13.1/13.3/13.4 exact output checks and Theorem 13.2 iff | `higham13_algorithm13_1_partitioned_lu_reconstructs`, `higham13_algorithm13_3_block_lu_reconstructs`, `higham13_algorithm13_4_recursive_partitioned_lu_reconstructs`, `blockMatrixIdentity`, `BlockMatrixTwoSidedInverse`, `BlockMatrixNonsingular`, `leadingBlockPrefix13_2`, `LeadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2`, `LeadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2.first_block_inverse`, `first_block_inverse_of_isUnit_det`, `BlockLUFactSpec.first_block_inverse_of_existsUnique`, `BlockLUFactSpec.schurTail_existsUnique_of_existsUnique_of_first_block_inverse`, `BlockLUFactSpec.existsUnique_of_leadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2`, `LeadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2.of_existsUnique`, `BlockLUFactSpec.existsUnique_iff_leadingPrincipalBlockNonsingular13_2` | The algorithm output checks prove exact source-step reconstruction. The one-block base case constructs `L = I`, `U = A`, proves `BlockLUFactSpec`, preserves the separate lower/upper budgets, and derives the Eq.13.22 product bound. ## Implementation Plan

1. Correct the Chapter 13 module metadata and source labels in `BlockLU.lean`.
2. Add source-facing theorem surfaces for all primary labels and equations, separating:
   - exact algebraic identities and definitions;
   - first-order floating-point model assumptions;
   - conditional aggregation lemmas that genuinely prove scalar consequences; and
   - open proof-source obligations for omitted external proofs.
   Current progress: first-order scalar assumption structures and matrix
   residual specs for the core Theorem 13.5 computed-operation models, gamma adapters,
   the Chapter 13 entrywise block-index max-norm convention bridge,
   the conventional matrix-multiplication `c1(m,n,p)=n^2` instance for (13.4)
   and conventional columnwise triangular-substitution `c2(m,p)=m^2` instances
   for (13.5),
   the block-LU-to-standard-LU product bridge,
   partition-display wrappers for (13.20) and (13.26),
   the SPD-section symmetric partition display,
   the Eq.13.19 norm-comparison assumption package,
   the Theorem 13.8 one-step `2 * max` block-bound corollary, active-stage
   column induction layer, and staged max-bound wrapper,
   the row block diagonal dominance large-`L` scalar-block family,
   the Problem 13.1 displayed block-tridiagonal norm-bound core,
   the Problem 13.2 finite 1-norm/infinity-norm incomparability witnesses,
   the Problem 13.3 scalar-block row-dominance/non-SPD counterexample,
   the Problem 13.5 point-column inverse-action bound,
   the row/transpose diagonal-dominance bridge, block-count recurrence adapters,
   the Theorem 13.5 scalar recurrence-instantiated proof step, its
   explicit `FirstOrderLe`/`+ O(u^2)` wrapper, and the
   residual-plus-recurrence package
   `higham13_theorem13_5_residual_and_recurrence_from_specs` /
   `higham13_theorem13_5_partitioned_step_spec_from_specs`,
   the Algorithm 13.3 Implementation 1/2 local computed-path specs
   `Algorithm13_3Implementation1LocalSpec` /
   `Algorithm13_3Implementation2ExplicitInverseSpec`,
   Eq.13.11a's exact additive proof-step identity, Eq.13.11b's scalar
   first-order trailing Schur error bound, the Eq.13.11 product/subtraction
   spec wrapper, Eq.13.13's exact trailing block
   identity and scalar first-order trailing block aggregation plus its
   product/subtraction/induction-spec wrapper,
   source-step reconstruction theorems for Algorithms 13.1/13.3/13.4,
   Problem 13.4 certificate bridges for the lower-left solve and Schur
   condition-number product, and exact scalar consequences for (13.22) and
   (13.25), exact Matrix adapters
   for equations (13.1)--(13.3), the Eq.13.18 one-step Schur column
   proof-chain wrappers, the row-wise one-step dominance inheritance theorem,
   and exact
   algebra adapters for Problems 13.7--13.9, have been added and compile.
3. Formalize the easier exact algebra first:
   - `BlockLUFactSpec` adapters;
   - Eq.13.1/Eq.13.2/Eq.13.3 Matrix.fromBlocks identities;
   - Problems 13.7--13.9 determinant/inverse identities, reusing Mathlib block matrix facts if available.
4. Formalize the block diagonal dominance infrastructure:
   - source-named Eq.13.17 gamma definitions;
   - row/column transpose bridge;
   - one-step Schur inheritance and growth bound refinements;
   - exact corollaries for Eq.13.19--Eq.13.23 where current helper lemmas already give scalar consequences.
5. Replace or quarantine the current vacuous SPD lemma adapters:
   - either prove Lemmas 13.9/13.10 from existing Cholesky/SPD infrastructure;
   - or leave the selected rows open with a not-proved ledger and do not count Eq.13.24/Eq.13.25 as closed.
6. Maintain proof-source ledger entries for Theorem 13.6 and any external proof imported from Demmel--Higham--Schreiber [326].
7. Update `docs/LIBRARY_LOOKUP.md`, `examples/LibraryLookup.lean`, and `.codex/PROJECT_MEMORY.md`.
8. Run:
   - `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LU/BlockLU.lean`
   - `lake env lean examples/LibraryLookup.lean`
   - `lake build`
   - `rg -n "\\b(sorry|admit|axiom|unsafe|opaque)\\b" LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LU/BlockLU.lean`

## Open Selected-Scope Items

All selected rows in `docs/CHAPTER13_SOURCE_INVENTORY.md` are considered open unless the inventory marks a current declaration as an acceptable exact closure. In particular, the current SPD lemma wrappers are not closures.

- The Problem 13.4 dominated history-envelope adapters, the one-block base cases, and the source-facing one-step/successor Eq.13.22/Eq.13.23 product/witness lifts are genuine local integration theorems, not closure of the recursive/global source row: the dominated adapters replace the three local containment hypotheses by the single explicit domination hypothesis `maxEntryNorm localGrowthEnvelope <= maxEntryNorm G`, the base cases construct `L = I`, `U = A` and prove the Eq.13.22/Eq.13.23 bounds for a `1 × 1` block matrix, the product lifts package the first split plus recursive tail hypotheses for `blockLUOneStepL/U`, the witness lifts add `BlockLUFactSpec` conclusions for those explicit factors under a Schur-tail factorization hypothesis, the Eq.13.22 successor wrappers turn an existential Schur-tail budget witness into the corresponding separate-budget and product-bound successor witnesses, and the Eq.13.23 successor wrapper turns the same existential tail data plus `rho <= 2` into the corresponding product-bound successor witness. The exact-κ ambient-chain constructor wrappers additionally instantiate the base and first-split successor chain constructors from matrix-stage source data, and the tail-chain successor wrappers package concrete Eq.13.22/Eq.13.23 factors from a supplied recursive tail chain. The remaining selected-scope theorem is the recursive source-tail chain/lift to the full factors; Eq.13.23 then also needs the source proof of `rho <= 2` at the final recursive surface.
- The ambient-budget chain `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_norms`, `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.mono`, `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_product`, `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_eq13_22_product`, `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_eq13_23_product`, `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_eq13_22_product_exact_kappa`, and `Higham13BlockLUBudgetChain.exists_blockLUFact_eq13_23_product_exact_kappa` are the current recursive structural lift: if every Schur tail supplies compatible lower/upper budgets, Lean now constructs full `BlockLUFactSpec` factors satisfying those budgets, transports the chain to larger ambient budgets, packages the product bound `‖L‖‖U‖ <= C_L*C_U`, and specializes it to the displayed Eq.13.22/Eq.13.23 constants when the chain is supplied with the source budgets.
